{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","updatedTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","title":"Trump suggests deploying the National Guard in Wisconsin, seemingly unaware that it's already been done","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-deploy-wisconsin-national-guard-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f45ad4189aff80028ab7efd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"donald trump\" height=\"2401\" width=\"4803\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump talks to reporters in the Oval Office at the White House July 20, 2020 in Washington, D.C.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Doug Mills-Pool/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>President Donald Trump on Tuesday did not appear to be aware of Wisconsin's official response to the state's ongoing <a href=\"http://www.insider.com/category/jacob-blake\">Jacob Blake</a> protests.</li><li>Trump suggested the governor ought to activate the National Guard, which was already done on Monday.</li><li>Gov. Tony Evers activated the state's National Guard assets following the protests in the wake of the Jacob Blake shooting.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>President Donald Trump on Tuesday did not appear to be aware of Wisconsin's official response to the ongoing <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/jacob-blakes-mother-we-need-healing-powerful-speech-about-son-2020-8\">Jacob Blake</a> protests and suggested the governor ought to activate the National Guard, which was already done on Monday.</p><p>\"Governor should call in the National Guard in Wisconsin,\" Trump <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1298414089769750530?s=20\">tweeted</a> Tuesday evening. \"It is ready, willing, and more than able. End problem FAST!\"</p><p>Despite Trump's recent suggestion, Democratic Gov. Tony Evers had already activated the National Guard to support local law enforcement at the request of local officials. Evers activated the state's National Guard assets following the protests in the wake of the Jacob Blake shooting.</p><p>Blake, a 29-year-old Black man in Kenosha, Wisconsin, was shot seven times by police officers on Sunday, and is now paralyzed from the waist down, according to his father. Video footage of the shooting was recorded and distributed on social media channels, prompting outrage across the nation.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f44dddb42f43f001ddfecc1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"kenosha police jacob blake wisconsin\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jacob Blake lies on the street after he got shot following a police shooting in Kenosha, Wisconsin, August 23, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Incident Response/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Following the protests, city officials declared a state of emergency and imposed a curfew. Gov. Evers initially activated around 125 Guardsmembers to assist first responders, but later increased that number \"to ensure individuals can exercise their right safely, protect safe buildings and critical infrastructure, and support first responders and fire fighters.\"</p><p>In a separate statement on Monday, Evers noted that National Guard assets would not be used \"to impede the ability of people to peacefully protest or impede the ability of the media to report on this situation.\"</p><p>\"I know folks across our state will be making their voices heard in Kenosha and in communities across Wisconsin,\" Evers said in his statement. \"Every person should be able to express their anger and frustration by exercising their First Amendment rights and report on these calls to action without any fear of being unsafe.\"</p><p>Trump has frequently urged state governors to utilize their state-military assets in responding to largely civil protests. During the George Floyd protests, Trump was overheard in a <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-governors-george-floyd-protests/2020/06/01/430a6226-a421-11ea-b619-3f9133bbb482_story.html\">leaked conference call</a> disparaging governors by calling them \"weak,\" and suggesting they take control of the situation by using uniformed troops.</p><p>\"You have to dominate,\" Trump said, according to a recording obtained by The Washington Post. \"If you don't dominate, you're wasting your time. They're going to run over you. You're going to look like a bunch of jerks.\"</p><p>Gov. Evers previously declined Trump's offer of using federalized active-duty troops to quell the protests in his state. In a <a href=\"https://www.tmj4.com/news/local-news/not-welcome-in-wisconsin-gov-tony-evers-writes-letter-to-president-trump-criticizing-plan-to-send-federal-agents-to-milwaukee\">letter</a> last month, Evers said he was strongly opposed to \"any such intervention,\" adding that \"this excessive and unwelcome federal law enforcement presence only makes these situations more volatile and dangerous.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-deploy-wisconsin-national-guard-2020-8'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"summary-list\">\n <li>In Washington, DC, a group of protesters at a Black Lives Matter action yelled at patrons of a restaurant, with video of the incident then going viral.</li>\n <li>Left and right were in rare agreement: yelling at random people is not an effective means of protesting injustice.</li>\n <li>But some commentators went further than the evidence, suggesting an incident was emblematic of the broader Black Lives Matter movement.</li>\n <li>In the meantime, the police killings that revived protests over the summer continue: at least 1,021 people have been killed by US law enforcement over the past year.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>People protesting the <a href=\"http://www.insider.com/category/jacob-blake\">police shooting of Kenosha, Wisconsin, man Jacob Blake</a> were caught on video berating two women sitting outdoors at a restaurant in a gentrified neighborhood in Washington, DC, on Monday night.</p>\n<p>The episode, documented by The Washington Post's Frederick Kunkle, showed a group of white protesters yelling at a woman at a restaurant patio in Adams Morgan who declined to raise her fist in solidarity with them.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">\n —Fredrick Kunkle WaPo (@KunkleFredrick) \n <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1298344285079838720?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 25, 2020</a>\n</blockquote>\n<script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n<p>Across television and social media, critics from both the left and right lamented the incident.</p>\n<p>\"The American left in action, 2020,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/brithume/status/1298398018924875776\">wrote</a> Fox News TV personality Brit Hume. His colleague, Tucker Carlson, dutifully aired a segment regarding the 30-second clip, portraying it as emblematic of the broader national movement against racism.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">\n —Justin Baragona (@justinbaragona) \n <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1298415506219769858?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 26, 2020</a>\n</blockquote>\n<script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>\"Pretty sure everyone has said all there is to say about this,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/byjoelanderson/status/1298375534028574720\">tweeted</a>&nbsp;Joel D. Anderson, a columnist at Slate, \"but I can't help but think we'd be better off if white people did some version of this at home to their racist mothers and uncles and old college buddies.\"</p>\n<p>\"White people continuing to do the most and least simultaneously,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/marclamonthill/status/1298422440452853766\">added Marc Lamont Hill</a>, a professor at Temple University.</p>\n<p>\"This is why white people taking over our movements is actually bad,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/queerBengali/status/1298406647891742728\">said activist Monjula Ray</a>. \"They never know when to take a f---ing seat.\"</p>\n<p>Lauren B. Victor, the urban planner to whom the shouts were directed, told the Post she wasn't afraid when it happened, just uncomfortable with the mob mentality. \"I'm very much with them,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/KunkleFredrick/status/1298344285079838720\">she said</a>. \"I've been marching with them for weeks and weeks and weeks.\"</p>\n<p>Victor was one of several restaurant patrons who were approached by protesters over the evening. As the crowd of people wound through the Columbia Heights neighborhood they could be heard shouting: \"Fire, fire, gentrifier — Black people used to live here.\"</p>\n<p>On Tuesday, protests against police violence continued for the third night. Over the past year, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/graphics/investigations/police-shootings-database/\">1,021 people</a>, disproportionately Black and Latino, have been shot and killed by police.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip? Davis)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f45c74c42f43f001ddff0c0?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn26@2020_2/2020/08/26/09-00-52-372_13c8422de3bfe715.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn33@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-52-638_00f09200df8426be.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=yifvId3-lgs:fc9BHaDh1XI:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn38@2020_4/2020/08/26/09-00-54-857_63cc81eddb437379.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=yifvId3-lgs:fc9BHaDh1XI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn25@2020_5/2020/08/26/09-00-49-736_4d6b112cc86ef56d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=yifvId3-lgs:fc9BHaDh1XI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn37@2020_1/2020/08/26/09-00-56-807_9d0836e59ac2eb08.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=cGdyc7Q-1BI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn13@2020_5/2020/08/26/09-00-52-311_767e235117808cfa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=QXVau8BzmBE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn90@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-51-477_edf0fa9b5dde1c97.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/clusterstock/~4/yifvId3-lgs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn85@2020_5/2020/08/26/09-00-45-119_0780a23f122ae2ec.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598432350846},{"createdTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","updatedTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","title":"Secretary of State Mike Pompeo made a series of false claims about Trump's foreign policy in controversial RNC speech","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/pompeo-rnc-speech-jerusalsem-israel-video-hatch-act-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f45733d42f43f001ddfefd3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mike Pompeo\" height=\"750\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gabriel Kuchta/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>Secretary of State Mike Pompeo controversially delivered a speech on the second night of the Republican National Convention while on a taxpayer-funded diplomatic trip to Israel.</li><li>Pompeo's remarks broke from protocol, as secretaries of state don't typically address political conventions and are meant to avoid engaging in domestic politics while abroad.</li><li>Democrats, ethics watchdogs, and diplomats excoriated Pompeo's unprecedented speech.</li><li>Much of what Pompeo said on Tuesday was at odds with reality, as he repeatedly embellished what Trump has accomplished in terms of foreign policy.&#160;</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"f0e80ded5d35b2778c5da3bdda2e6898\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>Secretary of State Mike Pompeo delivered pre-taped remarks from Jerusalem on the second night of the Republican National Convention, breaking a longstanding precedent and facing accusations of breaking the law in the process.</p><p>Though Pompeo issued a warning to US diplomats just last month against becoming involved in the \"political process,\" America's top diplomat seemingly broke from his own guidance and endorsed President Donald Trump for a second term on Tuesday.</p><p>\"President Trump understands what my great fellow Kansan, President Eisenhower said: 'For all that we cherish and justly desire for ourselves or for our children, the securing of peace is the first requisite,'\" Pompeo said in his speech.</p><p>\"Delivering on this duty to keep us safe and our freedoms intact, this president has led bold initiatives in nearly every corner of the world. In China, he's pulled back the curtain on the predatory aggression of the Chinese Communist Party. The president has held China accountable for covering up the China virus and allowing it to spread death and economic destruction in America and around the world,\" Pompeo said.&#160;</p><p>The secretary of state went on to tout what he saw as Trump's foreign policy accomplishments, listing out an array of policy decisions and actions. This included Trump's decision to order the drone strike that killed top Iranian Maj. Gen. Qassem Soleimani, a move that pushed the US and Iran <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-iran-near-brink-of-a-war-that-would-likely-devastate-both-sides-2019-5\">to the brink of war.</a></p><p>Much of what Pompeo said was at odds with reality. He claimed, for example, that \"NATO is stronger\" because of Trump. But the president has spent the past several years bashing the historic alliance while raising the nerves of US allies in the process, and he's repeatedly made misleading assertions <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-nato-budget-is-funded-2018-7\">about how NATO is funded.</a></p><p>At another point, Pompeo said, \"In North Korea, the president lowered the temperature and against all odds, got the North Korean leadership to the table.\"</p><p>But the primary point of Trump sitting down with North Korean leader Kim Jong Un was to get the rogue state to denuclearize, which <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bolton-trump-wanted-pompeo-kim-jong-un-rocket-man-cd-2020-6\">it has not yet done</a> as it continues to engage in aggressive activities that have made US allies in the region uneasy.&#160;</p><p>\"The president exited the US from the disastrous nuclear deal with Iran and squeezed the ayatollah, Hezbollah, and Hamas,\" Pompeo said. \"The president, too, moved the US embassy to this very city of god, Jerusalem, the rightful capital of the Jewish homeland.\"</p><p>Pompeo did not discuss the fact that the decision to withdraw from the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/iran-nuclear-deal-explained\">Iran nuclear deal</a> was condemned by US allies and opened the door for the Iranians to pull away from the landmark pact while increasing tensions between Tehran and Washington. Also left unsaid was how controversial it was for Trump to move the US embassy to Jerusalem. Top regional experts repeatedly warned that doing so would be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jared-kushner-speech-jerusalem-embassy-opening-2018-5\">counterproductive to the longstanding US goal of a two-state solution</a> to the Israel-Palestine conflict.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Axios  (@axios) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1298450448094027776?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 26, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>It's unusual for America's top diplomat to address political conventions, and against protocol for secretaries of state to inject themselves in domestic politics while abroad and acting in an official capacity.&#160;</p><p>Pompeo's unprecedented decision to deliver a partisan speech on a taxpayer-funded trip to the Middle East has sparked uproar among congressional Democrats, diplomats, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ethics-experts-slam-pompeo-for-appearing-at-rnc-from-israel-2020-8\">and ethics watchdogs.</a> It was the first time in at least 75 years a sitting secretary of state has spoken at a political convention.</p><p>\"At a time when peace and security in Middle East is so tough, Jerusalem should not be a prop for the RNC, and @SecPompeo should not be tarnishing the office of SecState. Unprecedented and wrong,\" veteran diplomat Wendy Sherman <a href=\"https://twitter.com/wendyrsherman/status/1297654145604780034?s=20\">tweeted</a> on Sunday.&#160;</p><p>Democrats have suggested that Pompeo's speech was illegal and in violation of the Hatch Act &#8212; a federal law that prohibits federal employees, other than the president, from engaging in political activities (including campaigning) while on the job.&#160;</p><p>Accordingly, the Democratic-led House is investigating Pompeo's RNC speech.&#160;</p><p>Former Vice President Joe Biden's campaign decried Pompeo's speech as an \"abuse of taxpayer dollars,\" adding that \"it undermines the critical work being done by the State Department.\"&#160;</p><p>The State Department, however, has defended Pompeo's decision to deliver an RNC speech, contending that he appeared at the convention in a personal capacity. The department said that no taxpayer funds were used in the production of the video.&#160;</p><p>Pompeo has been a long-serving member of Trump's tumultuous cabinet. He's among Trump's most loyal advisers, and has often clashed with the media.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a class=\"summary-list\"><li>Coronavirus cases in the US overall are declining but experts worry as the regions in the middle of the country experience surges and students return to Midwest may see an uptick in cases as students return to college.&#160;</p><p>\"The next area of tremendous concern is the Midwest and Upper Midwest. It is clear now that from Indiana, through Ohio and into Kentucky and Missouri, as well as northward into Illinois and Michigan, there is a substantial increased risk throughout the region,\" a <a href=\"https://policylab.chop.edu/blog/covid-19-outlook-shifting-winds-and-inconsistent-signals\">report</a> from PolicyLab at Children's Hospital of Philadelphia said in late July.&#160;</p><p>Data from John Hopkins shows that in Kansas, the weekly average of daily cases on Monday increased by 100 from mid-June to 561.&#160;</p><p>Kansas Gov. Laura Kelly told <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/world-nation/story/2020-08-25/new-coronavirus-cases-decline-us-experts-masks\">CNN</a>&#160;that the state hit an \"unfortunate milestone\" now that every county has reported a case, and infections are going up. Kelly also expressed concern over clusters of cases reported at universities as they reopen.&#160;</p><p>The University of Kansas reported over 80 COVID-19 cases last week, CNN reported.&#160;</p><p>Coronavirus clusters have been reported on several US campuses, including the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/6-days-reopening-u-of-a-over-500-coronavirus-cases-2020-8\">566 COVID-19 cases at the University of Alabama</a>, just six days after the campus re-opened.&#160;</p><p>The US is reporting around 43,000 new cases daily, a 21% decrease from the beginning of this month, according to data from <a href=\"https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/us-map\">John Hopkins University</a>.&#160;</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/world-nation/story/2020-08-25/new-coronavirus-cases-decline-us-experts-masks\">Los Angeles Times</a> reported that experts credit the reduced infections partly to people wearing masks.</p><p>\"It's profoundly hopeful news,\" Dr. Monica Gandhi, an infectious-diseases expert at UC San Francisco, told the Times.&#160;</p><p>Gandhi told the outlet that the public's growing understanding of how the virus spreads, better adherence to mask-wearing and a potential increase in the level of immunity are contributing to the decreased rate across the country.&#160;</p><p>So far, the US has recorded more than 5.7 million cases with over 178,000 deaths.&#160;</p><p>US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention Director Dr. Robert Redfield warned last week that while cases may be declining in previous hotspots in the South and West regions of the country, they're picking up in Middle America.&#160;</p><p>Hard-hit states like Florida are seeing marked decreases in cases. The state reported 2,600 new virus cases Tuesday compared to the 10,000 new cases it was regularly reporting earlier summer.&#160;</p><p>\"That is why it's so important for Middle America to recognize the mitigation that we talked about ... it's for Middle America too, the Nebraskas, the Oklahomas,\" US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention Director Dr. Robert Redfield told CNN. \"We don't need to have a third wave in the heartland right now.\"</p><p>Dr. Anthony Fauci, the nation's leading infectious disease expert, echoed Redfield's concerns, warning that the Midwest could see a rise in cases if officials in those states don't implement measures to help curb the spread.</p><p>\"Some states are not doing that,\" Fauci told <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2020/07/28/896152597/midwest-could-see-surge-in-covid-19-cases-unless-states-are-more-careful-fauci-w\">NPR</a> about states who aren't taking proper guidelines. \"We would hope that they all now rethink what happens when you don't adhere to that. We've seen it in plain sight in the Southern states that surged. class=\"summary-list\">\n <li>President Trump has invited Marjorie Taylor Greene, a congressional candidate who has promoted the QAnon conspiracy hoax, to come to the White House.</li>\n <li>\"I'm Rep. Denver Riggleman, a Republican from Virginia, said Tuesday.</li>\n <li>Also on Tuesday, another Republican speaker, Mary Ann Mendoza, shared a Twitter thread from a QAnon conspiracy theorist alleging a Jewish plot to control the world, <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/rnc-speaker-boosts-qanon-conspiracy-theory-about-jewish-plot-to-enslave-the-world-1\">The Daily Beast reported</a>.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>President Donald Trump has invited a supporter of the QAnon conspiracy theory to attend his speech for the Republican National Convention, a move that comes the same day that a bipartisan congressional resolution was introduced condemning the deranged hoax.</p>\n<p>\"I'm honored and thrilled to be invited to attend President Trump's acceptance speech Thursday evening at the White House,\" Marjorie Taylor Greene, a congressional candidate in Georgia, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mtgreenee/status/1298349981083013121\">tweeted on Tuesday</a>.</p>\n<p>A source <a href=\"https://newsroom.ap.org/detail/TheLatestQAnon-backingcandidategetsWhiteHouseinvite/cbc6ea299f071fa193a76d977a9d743b/text?hpSectionId=d69e4f8a6c0a46c38da332e439a42f00&amp;st=hpsection&amp;mediaType=text,photo,video,graphic,audio&amp;dateRange=Anytime&amp;totalCount=21&amp;currentItemNo=1&amp;currentItemNo=1\">told the Associated Press</a> that the invite is legitimate.</p>\n<p>Greene has expressed support for QAnon, a set of conspiracy theories that hinges on claims from an anonymous online account that purports to have inside dirt on the workings of government (and the \"deep state\" it claims is thwarting Trump's agenda).</p>\n<p>\"Q is a patriot, we know that for sure,\" she said in a 2017 video, <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/08/12/901628541/qanon-supporter-who-made-bigoted-videos-wins-ga-primary-likely-heading-to-congre\">as NPR reported</a>. Referring to Trump, Greene said: \"There's a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity to take this global cabal of Satan-worshipping pedophiles out, and I think we have the president to do it.\"</p>\n<p>Despite repeatedly posting inaccurate claims — in 2017, it asserted that Hillary Clinton's arrest was imminent — QAnon has attracted ever more support. Its chief assertion these days is that President Donald Trump is covertly fighting an elite pedophile ring, despite said president's past friendship with Jeffrey Epstein and public support for Ghislaine Maxwell, who faces multiple charges related to Epstein's sexual abuse of young people.</p>\n<p>In July, the Combatting Terrorism Center at West Point described the conspiracy theory as a threat to national security, noting that \"QAnon has contributed to the radicalization of several people to notable criminal acts or acts of violence,\" <a href=\"https://www.politifact.com/factchecks/2020/aug/24/greg-gutfeld/qanon-hoax-has-been-linked-violence-fox-news-greg-/\">as PolitiFact reported</a>.</p>\n<p>The danger posed by self-righteous extremists has led some Republicans to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-praises-qanon-conspiracists-because-they-like-me-very-much-2020-8\">go against the president and condemn the hoax and the movement behind it.</a>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>\"QAnon and the conspiracy theories it promotes are a danger and a threat that has no place in our country's politics,\" Rep. Denver Riggleman, a Republican from Virginia, said Tuesday. Riggleman has introduced a bipartisan resolution condemning QAnon and asking the Federal Bureau of Investigation to keep an eye on \"extremists motivated by fringe political conspiracy theories,\" according to <a href=\"https://malinowski.house.gov/media/press-releases/representative-malinowski-introduces-bipartisan-resolution-condemning-qanon\">a press release</a>.</p>\n<p>\"I condemn this movement and urge all Americans to join me in taking this step to exclude them and other extreme conspiracy theories from the national discourse,\" Riggleman said.</p>\n<p>Organizers of the Republican National Convention, however, appear to agree with the president: Hours before she was set to address the RNC, one speaker, Mary Ann Mendoza, urged her Twitter followers to check out the anti-Semitic ravings of a QAnon conspiracy theorist who asserted that Jews are seeking to destabilize and control the world, <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/rnc-speaker-boosts-qanon-conspiracy-theory-about-jewish-plot-to-enslave-the-world-1\">The Daily Beast reported</a>.</p>\n<p>Mendoza was later pulled from the RNC's Tuesday night lineup, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/kaitlancollins/status/1298411155006906368\">CNN reported</a>.</p>\n<p>Neither the Trump campaign nor the Republican Party immediately returned requests for comment.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip? Lamarque/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>The second night of the 2020 Republican National Convention was a made-for-TV affair featuring a naturalization and pardoning ceremony.&#160;</li><li>President Donald Trump used the power of the presidency to promote his reelection campaign, in a blatant attempt to make himself look good on issues he's often criticized over: immigration and criminal justice.&#160;</li><li>Meanwhile, the night featured several fringe right-wing figures who pushed conspiracy theories and previously disproven talking points on a wide array of issues.&#160;</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"f0e80ded5d35b2778c5da3bdda2e6898\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>The second night of the Republican National Convention featured fringe right-wing figures pushing conspiracy theories and debunked talking points on a wide array of issues.&#160;</p><p>The GOP convention typically attracts the biggest conservative names in the country. That has not been the case for the 2020 convention, as President Donald Trump has so alienated prominent GOP establishment figures that some even chose to speak on Joe Biden's behalf at the Democratic National Convention last week instead.&#160;</p><p>Tuesday night's RNC lineup included several names most Americans have likely never heard of. People like Abby Johnson, an anti-abortion activist who supports <a href=\"https://twitter.com/kasie/status/1298429588708757504?s=20\">barring women from voting</a> and recently condoned police racially profiling her biracial son.&#160;</p><p>Nicholas Sandmann, a teenager who last year found himself at the center of a culture battle that largely played out on social media, was also a speaker. Sandmann used his speech to decry the media, and declared that he had been \"cancelled.\"</p><p>Former Florida Attorney General Pam Bondi offered a speech full of conspiracy theories on the Bidens and Ukraine that have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ukraine-gas-company-burisma-holdings-joe-bidens-son-hunter-explained-2019-9?utmSource=twitter&utmContent=referral&utmTerm=topbar&referrer=twitterrrer=twitter\">repeatedly been disproven.</a></p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;NowThis  (@nowthisnews) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1298435980857352194?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 26, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>One of the people slated to speak, Mary Ann Mendoza, had her speech cancelled at the last minute because she'd shared an <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/2020/8/25/21401858/rnc-canceled-mary-ann-mendoza-anti-semitic-conspiracy-theory-protocols-elders-zion\">anti-Semitic conspiracy theory</a> on Twitter earlier in the day.</p><p>While the second night of the RNC lacked the fire and fury of the first night of the proceedings, it filled that void with a series of surreal acts.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Trump, a president who has consistently vilified immigrants, returned to his roots as an entertainer and held a reality TV-style naturalization ceremony with acting Homeland Security chief Chad Wolf.</p><p>Five people became US citizens in the process, but what was not mentioned during that made-for-TV-moment was the fact Trump has separated thousands of migrant children from their parents, consistently sought to build a wall on the border to keep immigrants out, and routinely espoused xenophobic sentiments.&#160;</p><p>Trump, who recently sparked uproar after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/who-has-trump-pardoned-so-far-arpaio-johnson-scooter-libby-2018-5\">commuting the sentence of his friend Roger Stone</a>, also held a pardoning ceremony during the RNC on Tuesday. The \"law and order\" president, who has spent the summer demonizing people protesting systemic racism in America's criminal justice system, pardoned a convicted bank robber.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"none\">&#8212;Aaron Rupar  (@atrupar) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1298441939625410563?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 26, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>The naturalization and pardoning ceremonies both took place at the White House. The president has faced fierce criticism for holding much of the convention at the White House and politicizing what is perhaps the most iconic public building in the US.</p><p>In using the powers of his office to promote his reelection effort in such a blatant fashion, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-abused-the-powers-of-the-presidency-a-the-republican-convention-2020-8\">Trump broke ethical norms in a profound way on Tuesday</a>. And by performing an official duty in what was a campaign event, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/myhlee/status/1298457513684336640?s=20\">Wolf may have violated a law (the Hatch Act)</a> prohibiting federal employees from engaging in political activities while on the job.&#160;</p><p>This all came before Secretary of State Mike Pompeo delivered an unprecedented speech that broke protocol and saw America's top diplomat participate in a partisan event while on a taxpayer-funded trip to the Middle East. Pompeo has also faced allegations of breaking the law by delivering remarks at the convention, and House Democrats are launching an investigation into his speech.&#160;</p><p>And in the final speech of the evening, First Lady Melania Trump touched on how how \"mean and manipulative social media can be.\" Left unsaid was the president's well-documented, almost hourly tendency to use Twitter as a weapon to spread disinformation and attack his opponents.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Students are limited to socially distanced gatherings of 10 or fewer people and risk interim suspension if they violate guidelines.</p><p>\"Let me remind you: organizations and individuals will be held accountable for their unsafe behaviors,\" Vice President for Student Life at OSU Melissa Shivers said in a <a href=\"https://safeandhealthy.osu.edu/messages/2020/08/21/we-can-do-together\">letter to students</a> on Friday. \"And remember that this is all about more than the individual. We all have one shot at this.\"</p><p>At Syracuse University in New York, 23 students were suspended for similar violations to the college's COVID safety protocols. The suspensions took place after a group of students gathered on the campus lawn Wednesday evening.</p><p>\"The world is watching, and they expect you to fail. Prove them wrong. Be better. Be adults. Think of someone other than yourself. And also, do not test the resolve of this university to take swift action to prioritize the health and well-being of our campus and Central New York community.,\" Vice Chancellor J. Michael Haynie said in a<a href=\"https://news.syr.edu/blog/2020/08/20/last-nights-selfish-and-reckless-behavior/\"> statement emailed</a> to the Syracuse University community on Thursday.&#160;</p><p>Haynie criticized students who \"selfishly jeopardized\" the ability for the university to continue with the fall semester on campus.&#160;</p><p>Schools across the country are grappling with the risks of bringing students back to campus. At the University of Alabama, more than 560 cases of coronavirus have been reported with 531 of them being at the flagship Tuscaloosa campus, the <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/education/2020/08/25/college-coronavirus-cases/\">Washington Post reported</a>.</p><p>\"The rise in COVID cases that we have seen in recent days is unacceptable and if unchecked threatens our ability to complete the semester on campus. Now is the time for action,\" University of Alabama President Stuart Bell said in a <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=792rL8ydio4&feature=youtu.be&sf127307858=1307858=1\">press conference</a> on Monday.</p><p>Some universities are pulling back from on-campus classes and moving to online instruction in response to the virus. Last week, UNC-Chapel Hill made national headlines with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-unc-went-from-leading-college-reopening-to-shutting-down-in-a-week-2020-8\">135 cases of the virus in only seven days</a>. The spike in cases prompted the university to move to all-remote instruction.&#160;</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/6-days-reopening-u-of-a-over-500-coronavirus-cases-2020-8\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">6 days after reopening, the University of Alabama has over 500 coronavirus cases. documents with the Securities and Exchange Commission for a public stock listing on the New York Stock Exchange, offering one of the first comprehensive looks at <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-ice-explainer-data-startup-2019-7#why-are-people-protesting-amazon-4\">the secretive data company's</a> financials and operations &#8212; as well as potential risks, which it said included criticisms from activists.</p><p>\"Our relationships with government customers and customers that are engaged in certain sensitive industries, including organizations whose products or activities are or are perceived to be harmful, has resulted in public criticism, including from political and social activists, and unfavorable coverage in the media,\" the filing says.</p><p>Activists have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-protest-palo-alto-activists-ice-contracts-2019-8\">repeatedly protested</a> Palantir's work with US Immigration and Customs Enforcement, which reportedly includes licensing software to ICE to build profiles and plan workplace raids of undocumented immigrants. Lawmakers also questioned its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lawmakers-question-palantir-coronavirus-tracking-contracts-hhs-ice-2020-6\">$24.9 million contract</a> with the Department of Health and Human Services to track the spread of COVID-19, asking whether the data is being used to help ICE deport immigrants.</p><p>\"Palantir is complicit in the surveillance, arrest and deportation of our communities through their work with ICE. Their S1 recognizes that these are risky contracts to take on. We're calling on investors everywhere not to invest when the IPO happens. An investment in Palantir only serves to profit off the continued surveillance &#38; exploitation of communities by ICE,\" Jacinta Gonzalez, a senior campaign director at Latinx and Chicanx organizing group Mijente, told Business Insider in a statement.</p><p>Palantir said that critiques of its work could \"engender dissatisfaction among potential and existing customers, investors, and employees.\"</p><p>But the company also said that addressing those critiques could also pose a threat to its business.</p><p>\"Conversely, being perceived as yielding to activism targeted at certain customers could damage our relationships with certain customers, including governments and government agencies with which we do business, whose views may or may not be aligned with those of political and social activists,\" the filing says.</p><p>Palantir relies heavily on government contracts and also on a small number of major clients. According to the filing, $345 million of the company's $742 million in revenue (46%) last year came from its government work, and its top three customers accounted for 28% of its total revenue.</p><p>In a letter to investors included in the filing, Palantir CEO Alex Karp defended the company's work with government clients, suggesting that it will not significantly adjust course or drop any contracts in response to activists' demands.</p><p>\"Our work and the use of our software present difficult questions... We embrace the complexity that comes from working in areas where the stakes are often very high and the choices may be imperfect,\" Karp wrote.</p><p>\"We have chosen sides, and we know that our partners value our commitment. We stand by them when it is convenient, and when it is not,\" he added.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f459e6e42f43f001ddff09c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Biogen conference Marriot Long Wharf Boston\" height=\"1310\" width=\"1746\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The conference, held at the Marriott Long Wharf in Boston, is believed to be an early super-spreader event.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Erin Clark/The Boston Globe via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>One conference held in Boston may be responsible for tens of thousands of coronavirus cases across the state, country, and even world, a <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.08.23.20178236v1\">new study published</a> online on Tuesday said.</li><li>The conference was hosted by&#160;<strong>Biogen at Marriott Long Wharf hotel on February 26 and 27, the <a href=\"https://www.bostonglobe.com/2020/08/25/business/biogen-conference-likely-led-20000-covid-19-cases-boston-area-researchers-say/\">Boston Globe</a> reported.</strong></li><li><strong>Initial reports only officially linked 99 cases in the Boston area to the conference.&#160;</strong></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>A Biogen conference hosted in Boston in late February may be responsible for tens of thousands of coronavirus cases, a <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.08.23.20178236v1\">new study published</a> online on Tuesday said.</p><p>The was held at the Marriott Long Wharf hotel on February 26 and 27, the <a href=\"https://www.bostonglobe.com/2020/08/25/business/biogen-conference-likely-led-20000-covid-19-cases-boston-area-researchers-say/\">Boston Globe</a> reported.&#160;</p><p>The New York Times <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/12/us/coronavirus-biogen-boston-superspreader.html\">reported</a> in April that senior executives from the drug company caught the virus and then traveled to other states, cities, and countries unknowingly carrying the virus.&#160;</p><p>\"The smartest people in health care and drug development &#8212; and they were completely oblivious to the biggest thing that was about to shatter their world,\" John Carroll, editor of Endpoints News, told the Times.&#160;</p><p>At the time, <a href=\"https://www.mass.gov/doc/covid-19-cases-in-massachusetts-as-of-march-26-2020/download\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the Massachusetts Department of Public Health</a> said 99 people who had either attended the conference or were in contact with someone who had, had tested positive for the virus in the state.&#160;</p><p>Biogen was criticized, at the time, for moving forward with the conference even though several officials attending were from European countries that already had documented coronavirus outbreaks.&#160;</p><p>The Times added that some of the first coronavirus cases in states like Indiana, Tennessee, and North Carolina were Biogen executives.&#160;</p><p>The study posted on Tuesday has yet to be peer-reviewed and published in a scientific journal. It also doesn't specifically refer to Biogen, referring to the conference as an \"international business conference held in Boston.\"</p><p>\"We're not trying to point fingers,\" Bronwyn MacInnis, director of pathogen surveillance told the Globe. \"Some [viral] introductions fizzle out, others light fires. The circumstances of this event ― the fact that it happened so early in the epidemic and the timing of where we were with COVID in the public consciousness ― meant it had a disproportionate effect. It happened in a city that wasn't 'woke.' \"</p><p>Researchers at the Broad Institute of Harvard and the Massachusetts Institute of Technology studied the genome of 772 coronavirus samples from people in Boston from January and May.&#160;</p><p>More than a third of the samples collected were infected with a strain of the virus that could be traced to the conference.&#160;</p><p>From the 289 cases that could be traced to the conference, 122 of the samples were from people living and working in Boston-area homeless shelters, the study reported.</p><p>\"I'm confident that the scale for measuring this event is in the tens of thousands,\" Dr. Jacob Lemieux, an infectious disease physician at Massachusetts General Hospital told the Globe.</p><p>Caroline Buckee, a professor of epidemiology at the Harvard T.H. Chan School of Public Health&#160; did not have anything to do with the study but told the Globe that the findings seem probable. She received a copy of the study before it appeared Tuesday on a preprint server.&#160;</p><p>\"Super-spreading is really a key component of how we ended up with an epidemic of this gravity,\" Buckee said. \"If you think about it, all the cases in the whole world originated from one case. That's the nature of the exponential growth of epidemics.\"</p><p>In an email statement, a Biogen spokesperson told Business Insider that they don't dispute the findings of the study, and have collaborated with the researchers.&#160;</p><p style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\"February 2020 was nearly a half year ago, and was a period when general knowledge about the coronavirus was limited. We were adhering closely to the prevailing official guidelines. We never would have knowingly put anyone at risk. When we learned a number of our colleagues were ill, we did not know the cause was COVID-19, but we immediately notified public health authorities and took steps to limit the spread,\" the company said.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/february-conference-boston-caused-thousands-covid-19-cases-2020-8'>Business Mattia/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>In SEC paperwork to go public, secretive data company Palantir revealed its CEO Alexander Karp made $12 million last year and had a travel stipend of $600,000.</li><li>Karp also was compensated for nearly $1 million for \"the person use of chartered aircraft.\"</li><li>Palantir filed IPO paperwork the day after a slew of unicorn-status enterprise tech startups filed to go public.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>Palantir CEO Alex Karp received a hefty $12 million in compensation last year, including a $600,000 travel stipend.&#160;</p><p>Karp's travel allowance &#8212; paid out in quarterly installments &#8212; was bumped up to $800,000 this year, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-direct-listing-s-1-prospectus-revealed-ahead-public-trading-2020-8\">the company revealed in its paperwork for a public listing on Tuesday.&#160;</a></p><p>With the coronavirus pandemic having shut down most of the world however, it's unclear where Karp will be travelling to.&#160;</p><p>Palantir noted in its S-1 that it has stopped all non-essential business travel by employees because of the pandemic. And the company even says it saved $1.4 million in the first six months of the year because of \"COVID-related travel restrictions\" and company-wide initiatives to decrease overall travel.</p><p>What that means for Karp's frequent journeys is not clear. In 2019, the company's 52-year-old cofounder and CEO, received $2.8 million in \"other compensation,\" including $1.46 million in personal security services as well as a substantial chunk for travel on personal trips and for commitments to other business roles not related to Palantir.</p><p>According to the S-1, Karp's expenses included $979,091 for \"the personal use of chartered aircraft pursuant to the aforementioned security program and incurred in connection with service on board of directors of other organizations and other personal travel.\"</p><p>Another $267,011 of that compensation was for \"other personal travel costs, including the use of corporate housing, incurred in connection with service on board of directors of other organizations\"</p><p>Karp is one of Palantir's 3 highest-paid executives listed in the S-1.&#160;</p><p>In 2019, President Stephen Cohen and Chief Operating Officer Shyam Sankar made $16 million and $25 million respectively.</p><div 4d05594d5629f5?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn57@2020_5/2020/08/26/09-00-57-337_d09786687d39f3ff.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn33@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-52-638_00f09200df8426be.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=ABHYSrH7W5A:Ah3SGlrNmLQ:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn2@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-45-974_0aa1ef8ce28369cc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=ABHYSrH7W5A:Ah3SGlrNmLQ:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn42@2020_3/2020/08/26/09-00-47-149_1a163f7fc5e8d003.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=ABHYSrH7W5A:Ah3SGlrNmLQ:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-46-959_49f45353dfff68fe.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=cGdyc7Q-1BI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn13@2020_5/2020/08/26/09-00-52-311_767e235117808cfa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=QXVau8BzmBE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn90@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-51-477_edf0fa9b5dde1c97.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/clusterstock/~4/ABHYSrH7W5A":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn41@2020_4/2020/08/26/09-00-56-943_9416b98df1aa52c8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598432350848},{"createdTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","updatedTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","title":"The Liberal Democrats are about to pick a new leader to revive the party after their 'really bad' general election result","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/liberal-democrats-new-leader-announcement-ed-davey-layla-moran-election-2020-8","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b509f4019032f1d008b47b1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Analysis banner\" height=\"61\" width=\"1201\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f44e8d889aff80028ab7b02?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Layla Moran Ed Davey\" height=\"514\" width=\"1028\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Layla Moran and Ed Davey.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ian Forsyth/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>Voting closes on Wednesday in the contest to be next leader of the Liberal Democrats.</li><li>Caretaker leader Ed Davey is the bookmakers' favourite in the race alongside fellow member of Parliament Layla Moran.</li><li>However, party sources say the contest is unpredictable and could be very close.</li><li>The new leader will face a huge challenge in rebuilding the party's confidence and purpose after the demoralising result of the December general election.</li><li>\"It wasn't just a bad result &#8212; it deflated what was a big return of optimism to the party and we have been struggling ever since,\" ex-leader Sir Vince Cable told Business Insider.</li><li>Both candidates agree that the Liberal Democrats should work with Labour leader Keir Starmer to defeat Boris Johnson's Conservatives.</li><li>The winner will be announced on Thursday morning.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>The Liberal Democrats will on Thursday announce their new leader as the pro-European party attempts to regain its confidence after a disappointing set of results in last December's UK general election.</p><p>After three months of campaigning, the party will on Thursday decide who should be tasked with breathing new life into the party after their anti-Brexit stance failed to make the sort of breakthrough many had predicted.</p><p>Either Ed Davey of Layla Moran will be announced as the new leader at 11:30 am and party figures believe the contest could be on a knife-edge as ballots close on Wednesday.</p><p>The party, encouraged by strong polling earlier in the year, went into December's election pledging to stop Brexit and hoping for major gains. However, despite increasing its vote share by over 4%, the Liberal Democrats ended up with one fewer seat in the House of Commons and then-leader Jo Swinson losing her own seat to Nicola Sturgeon's Scottish National Party.</p><p>Speaking to Business Insider this week, the party's former leader Sir Vince Cable said the result in December had crushed the party's spirit after \"spectacular\" results in local and European elections earlier in the year.</p><p>\"The party is not in a good place and it'd be dishonest and ridiculous to pretend it is,\" he told Insider.</p><p>\"The impact of the general election was really bad. It wasn't just a bad result &#8212; it deflated what was a big return of optimism to the party and we have been struggling ever since.\"</p><p>With the Liberal Democrats currently languishing at around 6% in the opinion polls, the victor faces a challenge in making the party relevant again.</p><p>Davey, a former carer, has vowed to make the Liberal Democrats the party of social care, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ed-davey-lib-dems-work-keir-starmer-defeat-boris-johnson-2020-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">describing</a> the Conservative government's handling of care homes during the coronavirus pandemic as \"negligence on a dramatic scale.\" Moran, who has warned the party that it faces a \"revival or irrelevance,\" wants to lead on education and has caught the eye with radical policies like Universal Basic Income. She also chairs an all-party parliamentary group on the government's response to the coronavirus ahead of a potential second wave this winter.</p><p>Sources close to Davey and Moran expect it to be close, with some suggesting the pair could be separated by just a few percentage points, with the result possibly as tight as the 2007 contest when Nick Clegg won by a margin of just 511 votes. A close result would represent a major turnaround for Moran, who in January was far behind Davey <a href=\"https://www.newstatesman.com/politics/uk/2020/01/ed-davey-ahead-liberal-democrat-leadership-race\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in a YouGov poll of members.</a></p><p>Davey, the party's caretaker leader, is the bookies' favourite having secured the backing of most of the party's MPs, including a surprise nomination from highly-rated Daisy Cooper. A member of Parliament of over 20 years and former minister in the last coalition government, Davey's pitch has focused on his campaigning experience. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ed-davey-lib-dems-work-keir-starmer-defeat-boris-johnson-2020-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">He told Business Insider</a> he was the best-placed candidate to \"get the party winning again\" after the disappointment of the snap election in December.</p><p>However, Moran says only she can deliver a clean break from the party's controversial past as unlike Davey, she did not serve in government with the Conservatives. Her campaign got off to a shaky start when <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moran-starmer-labour-should-fear-me-lib-dem-leader-2020-6?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in an interview with Business Insider,</a> she vowed to be \"more radical\" than the Labour Party, a statement that was seized on by opponents as a plan to be more left-wing than Labour. Sources close to the MP for Oxford West &#38; Abingdon say she has enjoyed momentum in the final few weeks of the campaign, winning over undecided members and previous backers of Davey.</p><p>However, party officials and both campaigns admit that in the absence of official polling of members, it is difficult to say with confidence exactly how the contest looks heading into the announcement on Thursday.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f44e86889aff80028ab7b00?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ed Davey Layla Moran\" height=\"729\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">PA/PA Images via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Cable told Business Insider he was \"genuinely torn\" over who to vote for. He said Davey was a \"very competent guy\" who is \"economically very literate\" and has a \"very good track record on environmental issues.\" However, he added that Moran is \"very good, very sparky,\" an \"impressive operator,\" and appeals to members \"who want a fresh, new approach,\" Cable said.</p><p>A major talking point during the contest has been how the Liberal Democrats should position itself in relation to the opposition Labour party. <a href=\"https://www.newstatesman.com/politics/uk/2020/07/where-next-liberal-democrats\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">As discussed in The New Statesman</a>, with the vast majority of seats the party can realistically win at the next election held by Conservatives, both Davey and Moran agree that the Liberal Democrats should be a centre-left party, taking the fight to what they see as a Conservative party that has lurched further to the right under Boris Johnson.</p><p>Cable told Business Insider that Starmer being Labour leader was a \"good thing\" for the Liberal Democrats as \"it's easier to function as an anti-Tory opposition party when you're dealing with a Labour Party that is electable.\"</p><p>\"One of the big problems we had at the December election was that in the target seats controlled by Conservatives, the dominant mood was 'we like the Lib Dems and agree with you on Europe, but we can't possibly risk having Corbyn run the government.' A lot of those soft Tory Remainers stuck with the Conservatives,\" he said.</p><p>Cable said the next leader of the Liberal Democrats should establish an \"implicit understanding\" with Labour that the priority at the next general election is defeating Conservative candidates, not each other. \"Our future with Labour is complimentary, not competitive,\" he said.</p><p>Both <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ed-davey-lib-dems-work-keir-starmer-defeat-boris-johnson-2020-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Davey</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moran-starmer-labour-should-fear-me-lib-dem-leader-2020-6?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Moran</a> told Business Insider that they'd be prepared to work with Labour leader Starmer to defeat the Conservatives at the next general election by encouraging tactical voting.</p><p>Whoever wins on Thursday will inherit a party scarred by December and faced with questions about its long-term viability. But as Liberal Democrat figures like to stress, the party is second in 91 seats and has four years to rebuild until the next general election. The challenge facing the new leader may be large, but it is not insurmountable.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Payne)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5b509f4019032f1d008b47b1?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn78@2020_1/2020/08/26/09-00-55-722_343d07670ae9555e.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f44e8d889aff80028ab7b02?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn33@2020_4/2020/08/26/09-00-46-922_16451b59effc6dcf.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f44e86889aff80028ab7b00?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/26/09-00-52-450_ad899e538c316012.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn33@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-52-638_00f09200df8426be.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=JDf1TUJiTB8:bYoffo-NATE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn2@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-51-736_7d0dd268c1e512f1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=JDf1TUJiTB8:bYoffo-NATE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn94@2020_2/2020/08/26/09-00-56-114_68d8bb10118abdfa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?i=JDf1TUJiTB8:bYoffo-NATE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn46@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-47-384_ddb08e62cfb43673.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=cGdyc7Q-1BI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn13@2020_5/2020/08/26/09-00-52-311_767e235117808cfa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/clusterstock?d=QXVau8BzmBE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn90@2020_6/2020/08/26/09-00-51-477_edf0fa9b5dde1c97.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/clusterstock/~4/JDf1TUJiTB8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn57@2020_4/2020/08/26/09-00-55-229_2ac5ebfbe873de4c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598432350848},{"createdTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","updatedTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","title":"Read the letter Palantir's CEO wrote attacking Silicon Valley companies as unpatriotic 'engineering elites' and allying itself with the Trump administration","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-s1-ipo-silicon-valley-military-tech-patriotic-alex-karp-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f458fb989aff80028ab7edd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Palantir\" height=\"1854\" width=\"2472\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Arnd Wiegmann/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>In its filing for a direct listing made public on Tuesday, secretive data-crunching firm Palantir is distancing itself from Silicon Valley &#8212; and pitching itself as a staunch ally to the US military and intelligence agencies.</li><li>Palantir, which has several high-profile contracts with agencies like the Pentagon and ICE, claimed in the filing that other tech companies were less loyal to US interests.</li><li>The document reflects Palantir's eagerness to position itself as adherent to President Donald Trump's foreign policy and national security worldview, a rarity in Silicon Valley.</li><li>\"We have chosen sides, and we know that our partners value our commitment,\" CEO Alex Karp wrote in a letter included in the filing.</li><li>Read the full letter below.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>Palantir started in Silicon Valley &#8212; but in its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-direct-listing-s-1-prospectus-revealed-ahead-public-trading-2020-8\">new filing to go public</a>, the company disavows its peers in the Bay Area.</p><p>\"The engineering elite of Silicon Valley may know more than most about building software. But they do not know more about how society should be organized or what justice requires,\" cofounder and CEO Alex Karp <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1321655/000119312520230013/d904406ds1.htm#rom904406_3\">wrote</a> in a letter included in the filing.&#160;</p><p>In the 17 years since it was founded, the secretive data-crunching firm has avoided the spotlight while racking up major contracts, primarily with government agencies like the Pentagon and ICE. Those contracts have drawn criticism, especially in the largely liberal Bay Area &#8212; and including from <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2019/08/22/war-inside-palantir-data-mining-firms-ties-ice-under-attack-by-employees/\">Palantir's own engineers</a>. But Karp and cofounder Peter Thiel, a megadonor and adviser to President Donald Trump, have repeatedly defended the contracts.</p><p>Now, Palantir is applying to go public in a direct listing &#8212; and its pitch to the public plays up its relationships with government agencies, depicting Silicon Valley tech companies as less patriotic. (The company recently <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-headquarters-hq-denver-palo-alto-silicon-valley-alex-karp-2020-8\">moved its headquarters</a> from Palo Alto to Denver, Colorado.) The filing also reflects Palantir's eagerness to position itself as uniquely adherent to Trump's foreign policy.</p><p>\"Our company was founded in Silicon Valley. But we seem to share fewer and fewer of the technology sector's values and commitments,\" Karp wrote in the letter. \"Our software is used to target terrorists and to keep soldiers safe ... We have chosen sides, and we know that our partners value our commitment.\"</p><p>Palantir's extensive contracts with government agencies, while controversial, are touted as a competitive strength in the company's S-1 filing. The company pitches itself as a staunch supporter of the US government's foreign policy interests.</p><p>\"Our software is used by the United States and its allies in Europe and around the world. Some companies work with the United States as well its adversaries. We do not. We believe that our government and commercial customers value this clarity,\" the company wrote.</p><p>The filing <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/palantir-s1-chinese-communist-party-2020-8\">slams other companies</a> for doing business with China, which it describes as an enemy to the US. Other tech giants like Apple, Google, Facebook, and Microsoft have <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/08/08/trump-tiktok-wechat-ban-echoes-other-countries-including-china.html\">previously pursued deals</a> with the Chinese government &#8212; something Palantir explicitly pledges not to do in its filing.&#160;</p><p>Palantir's pledge aligns with Trump's China agenda &#8212; the president himself has led a charge to sever relationships between China and US tech companies, including a recent <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/06/trump-signs-executive-orders-banning-transactions-with-tiktok-and-wechat/\">executive order</a> barring business transactions with ByteDance, which owns popular video app TikTok, and WeChat.</p><p>\"Our software is used by the United States and its allies in Europe and around the world. Some companies work with the United States as well its adversaries. We do not. We believe that our government and commercial customers value this clarity,\" the company wrote in the filing.</p><p>Read Karp's <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1321655/000119312520230013/d904406ds1.htm#rom904406_3\">full letter</a>, which introduced the company's S-1 and is divided into five parts, below:</p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our welfare and security depend on effective software.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>In times of stability, the right software helps our most critical institutions serve their markets and the public. In times of crisis, effective software can be essential to an organization's survival.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our software platforms are used by the United States and its allies around the world. Many of the world's most vital institutions, from defense and intelligence agencies to companies in the healthcare, energy, and manufacturing sectors, rely on the software platforms that we have built.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The challenges that we face, and the crises that we have and will continue to confront, expose the systemic weaknesses of the institutions on which we depend. Our industrial infrastructure and manufacturing supply chains were conceived of and constructed in a different century. Government agencies have faltered in fulfilling their mandates and serving the public. Some institutions will struggle to survive. Others will collapse.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our customers come to us because their technological infrastructure has failed them. The enterprise software industry's focus on custom software tools and applications is misplaced. Those approaches often only work briefly, if at all. The problems and needs of an organization often change before the software can even be deployed.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our partners require something more. They need generalizable platforms for modeling the world and making decisions. And that is what we have built.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>II.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our company is a creative enterprise, filled with strong personalities who are immensely talented and care deeply about their work.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The culture of our company is more than a mere byproduct of the people we choose to hire. Our culture and means of organizing ourselves are preconditions for the creation of effective software.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>We identify what needs to be done and organize ourselves around the outcomes that we hope to achieve. This requires that we stay flexible about who should be leading what and when.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>At many organizations, employees spend their days, even their careers, posturing for others, concerned with claiming credit for success and avoiding blame for failure.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Entire companies can subsist for years on a business model that may have made sense at some point in the past. In the short term, there are often profits to be extracted from the enterprise, and from customers.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>We have rejected this way of working. The alignment of interests between our employees and our company, and between our company and our customers, is one of the principal reasons we have come as far as we have.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>III.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our work and the use of our software present difficult questions.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The construction of software platforms that enable more effective surveillance by the state of its adversaries or that assist soldiers in executing attacks raises countless issues, involving the points of tension and tradeoffs between our collective security and individual privacy, the power of machines, and the types of lives we both want to and should lead. The ethical challenges that arise are constant and unrelenting.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>We embrace the complexity that comes from working in areas where the stakes are often very high and the choices may be imperfect.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The more fundamental issue is where authority to resolve such questions &#8212; to decide how technology may be used and by whom &#8212; should reside.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our society has effectively outsourced the building of software that makes our world possible to a small group of engineers in an isolated corner of the country. The question is whether we also want to outsource the adjudication of some of the most consequential moral and philosophical questions of our time.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The engineering elite of Silicon Valley may know more than most about building software. But they do not know more about how society should be organized or what justice requires.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>IV.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our company was founded in Silicon Valley. But we seem to share fewer and fewer of the technology sector's values and commitments.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>From the start, we have repeatedly turned down opportunities to sell, collect, or mine data. Other technology companies, including some of the largest in the world, have built their entire businesses on doing just that.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Software projects with our nation's defense and intelligence agencies, whose missions are to keep us safe, have become controversial, while companies built on advertising dollars are commonplace. For many consumer internet companies, our thoughts and inclinations, behaviors and browsing habits, are the product for sale. The slogans and marketing of many of the Valley's largest technology firms attempt to obscure this simple fact.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The world's largest consumer internet companies have never had greater access to the most intimate aspects of our lives. And the advance of their technologies has outpaced the development of the forms of political control that are capable of governing their use.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The bargain between the public and the technology sector has for the most part been consensual, in that the value of the products and services available seemed to outweigh the invasions of privacy that enabled their rise.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Americans will remain tolerant of the idiosyncrasies and excesses of the Valley only to the extent that technology companies are building something substantial that serves the public interest. The corporate form itself &#8212; that is, the privilege to engage in private enterprise &#8212; is a product of the state and would not exist without it.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Our software is used to target terrorists and to keep soldiers safe. If we are going to ask someone to put themselves in harm's way, we believe that we have a duty to give them what they need to do their job.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>We have chosen sides, and we know that our partners value our commitment. We stand by them when it is convenient, and when it is not.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>V.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The ability of our most vital institutions to protect and provide for the public requires the right technology.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>And we believe that as a result, over the long term, the strength and survival of democratic forms of government do as well.</em></p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>Alexander C. Karp, <br ></em><em>Chief Executive Officer&#160;&#38;&#160;Co-Founder<br ></em><em>Palantir Technologies Inc.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 16:59:10","updatedTime":"2020-08-26 16:59:10","title":"The CDC quietly modified coronavirus testing guidelines to exclude people who are asymptomatic, potentially limiting our understanding of the true scope of the virus","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-modified-covid-19-testing-guidelines-to-exclude-asymptomatic-people-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f458d5a42f43f001ddff083?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coronavirus test\" height=\"512\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A female doctor holds a swab in one of the central fairgrounds in the outpatient corona test facility.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/april-2020-berlin-a-female-doctor-holds-a-swab-in-one-of-news-photo/1210865862?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Britta Pedersen/picture alliance via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>The Center for Disease Control quietly <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/hcp/testing-overview.html\">modified its testing guidelines</a> on Monday and no longer requires people who are asymptomatic to get tested for the virus.&#160;</li><li>Experts are concerned this will hinder our understanding of the true scope of the outbreak in the US.&#160;</li><li>Last week, the World Health Organization said the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/who-coronavirus-being-transmitted-by-young-asymptomatic-people-2020-8\">virus is mainly being spread by young people who are unaware</a> that they are infected.&#160;</li><li>In July, the CDC itself said that <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/hcp/planning-scenarios.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"89ae91847e7947c9522a3fa9a5dcd20a\">40% of people infected with COVID-19 are asymptomatic</a> and that the transmission rate from those who show no symptoms was 75%.&#160;</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>People who are exposed to a person with coronavirus but are asymptomatic are no longer encouraged to get tested for the coronavirus, the Center for Disease Control said in <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/hcp/testing-overview.html\">subtly modified testing guidelines</a> released on Tuesday.&#160;</p><p>The CDC now says that anyone who has been within six feet of someone who has COVID-19 for at least 15 minutes, or is in a high coronavirus transmission area and has attended public or private gatherings for more than 10 people without widespread physical distancing and mask-wearing, is not required to test for the virus unless they're in an at-risk population.&#160;</p><p>As a caveat, the newly released guidelines also state: \"It is important to realize that you can be infected and spread the virus but feel well and have no symptoms.\"</p><p>Experts told&#160;&#160;<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/08/25/world/covid-19-coronavirus.html?action=click&module=Top%20Stories&pgtype=HomepageHomepage\">The New York Times</a> they're concerned about the revision because it's important to identify infection before there are symptoms as that's when people are most contagious.&#160;</p><p>Last week, the World Health Organization said the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/who-coronavirus-being-transmitted-by-young-asymptomatic-people-2020-8\">virus is mainly being spread by young people who are unaware</a> that they are infected.&#160;</p><p>\"The epidemic is changing,\" WHO's Western Pacific regional director, Takeshi Kasai, said at a virtual briefing <a href=\"https://uk.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-who/pandemic-now-driven-by-20s-30s-40s-group-many-asymptomatic-who-idUKKCN25E0AZ\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"66e139c93e8faea6ad4fd71de9c06bcd\">reported Reuters</a>.</p><p>\"People in their 20s, 30s, and 40s are increasingly driving the spread,\" he said. \"Many are unaware they are infected. This increases the risk of spillovers to the more vulnerable.\"</p><p>In July, the CDC itself estimated <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/hcp/planning-scenarios.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"89ae91847e7947c9522a3fa9a5dcd20a\">that 40% of people infected with COVID-19 are asymptomatic.</a>&#160; Additionally, the agency said that the chance of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-estimate-40-percent-infected-with-covid-19-asymptomatic-2020-7\">transmission from those who show no symptoms</a> was 75%.</p><p>\"This is potentially dangerous,\" Dr. Krutika Kuppalli, an infectious disease physician in Palo Alto, California told the Times.&#160;</p><p>Kuppalli said that restricting the testing just to those who are showing symptoms means&#160; \"you're not looking for a lot of people who are potential spreaders of disease.\"</p><p>Neither the CDC nor the Department of Health and Human Services responded to Business Insider's request for comment.</p><p>A representative from the HHS told the Times: \"The decision to be tested should be one made in collaboration with public health officials or your health care provider based on individual circumstances and the status of community spread.\"</p><p>&#160;</p><p>&#160;</p><p>&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
